"llsb","035","12480000.tif","035","001","s","","S. 378","18580519,18580607","Mr. Hamlin asked and, by unanimous consent, obtained leave to bring in the following bill; which was read twice and referred to the Committee on Public Lands. Committee discharged. A Bill To enable the Columbian College, in the District of Columbia, to found and establish a professorship of agricultural and mechanical science, and complete her endowment fund, and for the benefit of the public schools of Washington, District of Columbia. Whereas the Constitution of the United States gives to the Congress of the United States power of legislation for the people of the District of Columbia; And whereas said people have no other legislature, and, therefore, not only of right may, but of necessity must, look to Congress for all just measures of legislation; And whereas the people of said District of Columbia, in common with all other citizens of the United States, pay taxes upon imports into the treasury of the United States; And whereas the Constitution of the United States gives to Congress power to dispose of the territory of the United States; And whereas the Columbian College, in the said District of Columbia, proposes to establish a chair of agricultural and mechanical science, and also to admit, annually, four students, to be selected by the trustees of the public schools of the city of Washington, from among the best scholars educated at such schools, upon the ground and as the reward of extraordinary merit, to all the advantages of said college, including all the benefits to be derived from the establishment of said chair of agricultural and mechanical science, to be admitted and educated at said college free from all tuition and college charges: Therefore--","Committee on Public Lands"

"llsb","035","14990002.tif","035","002","s","2","S. 497","18590110,18590117,18590209","",""
"llsb","035","15000003.tif","035","002","s","3","S. 497","18590110,18590117,18590209","",""
"llsb","035","15010000.tif","035","002","s","","S. 497","18590209","Ordered to be printed. Amendment Intended to be proposed by Mr. Doolittle to the bill (S. 497) "making appropriation to facilitate the acquisition of Cuba by negotiation," viz; Strike out all after the enacting clause and insert the following: Whereas the proposition contained in the message of the President of the United States in relation to the purchase of the island of Cuba has already been considered and has been unanimously rejected by the Spanish government, and a resolution of the chamber of deputies, unanimously passed, and concurred in by all parties, has been ordered to be inscribed in their archives, and a similar resolution has also been passed by the senate, with such declarations, and accompanied by such language, as to demonstrate that any attempt by the government of the United States to purchase the island of Cuba at the present time would be not only unwise and impracticable, but offensive to the national pride of that government and people, and well calculated to induce that government to enter into treaties with France and England, by which she may engage never to cede that island to the United States, under any circumstances and for any consideration; and whereas, in the progress of events, from our geographical position and relations to the States of Mexico, Central and South America, and from our expanding commerce, important questions of national policy in relation to them are pressing upon us and must be met and determined; and whereas the policy recommended by the President in his annual message, and pursued by this administration, is well calculated to impress upon the people of these States a well grounded apprehension that it is the policy of this government to devote all its energies to the extension of slavery into those tropical regions, and such apprehension has alienated from the United States the people of all those States; and whereas it is our true policy to reassure them that the government of the United States will not pursue towards them any such policy, nor in any manner attempt to overturn their domestic policy by re-establishing slavery among them; and whereas the numerous disabilities to which free persons of color of African descent are subjected in many of the free States have made it desirable, on the part of large numbers of them, to seek elsewhere a more favorable field for their labor and enterprise; and whereas the same class of persons is regarded with still greater disfavor in the slave holding States, from considerations deemed so controlling that further emancipation in many of them has been prohibited by law, unless the persons emancipated shall be at the same time removed beyond the jurisdiction of the State, and in some of them the graver question is seriously entertained whether persons of African descent, who are now free, shall not again be reduced to slavery if they continue to remain within their jurisdictions; and whereas in Yucatan and Central and South America there are vast regions, almost uninhabited, of the most beautiful and productive countries in the world, in a climate well adapted to the constitution of the African race, to develop its greatest power and highest activity; and whereas it may possibly happen that an immediate payment of money will be called for by the stipulations of any treaty which may be entered into: Therefore--",""

Whereas reciprocal commercial intercourse among nations promotes mutual prosperity, and is the surest guarantee of permanent peace; and whereas it is not the policy of the United States to despoil any nation of her possessions, however rich or valuable, but to cultivate with all nations the most friendly and unrestricted commercial relations; and whereas the restrictive policy adopted by Spain against the trade and commerce of the United States with the Island of Cuba, forcing the adoption of a similar policy by the United States towards herself, impairs the benefits which would otherwise result to both nations from reciprocal trade and commerce between the United States and Cuba; and whereas treaty negotiation for the removal of all illiberal and unjust restrictions upon trade and commercial intercourse between this country and the Island of Cuba, and every nation upon this continent, is most desirable; therefore--",""

"llsb","035","15090000.tif","035","002","s","","S. 500","18590111","Mr. Mason, from the Committee on Foreign Relations, reported the following bill; which was read and passed to a second reading. A Bill Authorizing the President of the United States to use the public force of the United States in cases therein specified. Whereas, the President of the United States, in discharge of the duty imposed on him by the Constitution, "from time to time, [to] give to the Congress information of the state of the Union, and recommend to their consideration such measures as he shall judge necessary and expedient," has informed Congress, that by reason of the distracted and revolutionary condition of Mexico, of certain of the States of Central America, and occasionally of those in South America, as well the property as the lives and liberties of American citizens, peaceably and rightfully within their respective limits, are subjected to lawless violence or otherwise placed in peril by those claiming to be in authority, and for redress whereof negotiation and remonstrance in the forms of diplomatic intercourse are attempted in vain; and it being manifest to Congress that such condition of things in the States aforesaid will continue so long as government is found there in the unsettled and irresponsible condition, at present, and at times heretofore tolerated by their people; and it being the indispensable duty of the government of the United States, to protect its citizens against lawless violence without the limits of the United States whenever found on lawful errand: Therefore--","Committee on Foreign Relations"

"llsb","035","18210000.tif","035","002","s","","S. 591","18590218,18590219","Agreeably to notice, Mr. Stuart asked and obtained leave to bring in the following bill; which was read twice and referred to the Committee on Indian Affairs. Reported by Mr. Sebastian with an amendment, viz: Insert the section printed in italics. A Bill To carry out the Shawnee treaty of May ten, eighteen hundred and fifty-four. Whereas, in article nine of the Shawnee treaty of May ten, eighteen hundred and fifty-four, it is provided that "Congress may hereafter provide for the issuing to such of the Shawnees as may make separate selections patents for the same, with such guards and restrictions as may seem advisable for their protection therein;" and whereas "separate selections" have been made by many Shawnees fully competent to manage their affairs:","Committee on Indian Affairs"

"llsb","035","18330002.tif","035","002","s","2","S. 601","18590224","",""
"llsb","035","18340000.tif","035","002","s","","S. 602","18590224","Mr. Stuart, from the Committee on Public Lands, reported the following bill; which was read and passed to a second reading. A Bill For the relief of John B. Bennet. Whereas John B. Bennet, a mail contractor, did, in the month of January, eighteen hundred and fifty-six, contract to carry the mail of the United States from Highland, in Kansas Territory, through Nebraska Territory, to the mouth of the Nyoway river, in said Nebraska, in two-horse coaches, for a money consideration of three thousand five hundred dollars per annum, and the right, as was believed at the time, of pre-emption of mail stations to the extent of six hundred and forty acres of land for every twenty miles of the route, two hundred and twenty-seven miles, as provided for in the act of third March, eighteen hundred and fifty-five; and whereas, without this right of pre-emption, the price agreed upon was wholly inadequate for the service; and whereas the service was faithfully performed by the said John B. Bennet to the satisfaction of the Post Office Department; and whereas, by the construction placed upon the provision of said act of third March, eighteen hundred and fifty-five, granting pre-emption rights to mail contractors, by the Commissioner of the General Land Office, the said John B. Bennet is unable to obtain the pre-emption right to which he lays claim in virtue of his contract aforesaid and the provision of said act of third March, eighteen hundred and fifty-five; therefore--","Committee on Public Lands"
